      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText906888083355202654" style="display:none">Katherine V thought boys were gross<br />Katherine X just wanted to be friends<br />Katherine XVIII dumped him in an e-mail<br />K-19 broke his heart<br /><br />When it comes to relationships, Colin Singleton's type happens to be girls named Katherine. And when it comes to girls named Katherine, Colin is always getting dumped. Nineteen times, to be exact.<br /><br />On a road trip miles from home, this anagram-happy, washed-up child prodigy has ten thousand dollars in his pocket, a bloodthirsty feral hog on his trail, and an overweight, Judge Judy-loving best friend riding shotgun--but no Katherines. Colin is on a mission to prove The Theorem of Underlying Katherine Predictability, which he hopes will predict the future of any relationship, avenge Dumpees everywhere, and finally win him the girl.<br /><br />Love, friendship, and a dead Austro-Hungarian archduke add up to surprising and heart-changing conclusions in this ingeniously layered comic novel about reinventing oneself.</span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/859203-raleigh-rand"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442955040i/859203._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/859203-raleigh-rand">Raleigh Rand</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Colin was annoying but started to become endearing. I loved it when Hassan told him how selfish he was then later decided that he (Hassan) was the sel<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Colin was annoying but started to become endearing. I loved it when Hassan told him how selfish he was then later decided that he (Hassan) was the selfish one. He was right on both accounts. Colin really wants to be normal. Not really a genius or a prodigy. He just wants to be normal. We know this because he follows Hassan's cues as to what to how to act normal. Hassan tells him this is the way to act and no, never say that. So Colin is happy to follow the guidelines. He wants guidelines, as opposed to what his father wants and that is for Colin to be more than he ever was, and to be a genius. Colin is trying hard to live up to his father's expectations. The roadtrip ends up being wonderful for him because he finally finds himself. Away from his hovering, over-expectant parents. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

Just a quick question. Is Colin&#39;s whining REALLY that bad? 

F</a>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/16040782-paakhi"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1471244718i/16040782._UY100_CR38,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/16040782-paakhi">Paakhi</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I actually found his whining justifiable, given the circumstances he was in. I mean he had been dumped by eighteen Katherines, he wasn't prodigy and h<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I actually found his whining justifiable, given the circumstances he was in. I mean he had been dumped by eighteen Katherines, he wasn't prodigy and he thought he's never be a genius and he also had the chronic disease of wanting to matter to the world. I feel the every protagonist John writes about wants to matter, but anyway, I think Collin's whining isn't bad. <br />After thinking about it, he doesn't really whine that much. And Hassan always makes everything funny anyway, so. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228796955?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megs ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megs ♥" href="/user/show/5691412-megs">Megs ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=z-2012-reads">z-2012-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228796955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1698488357328410519"><br/>This was by far the worst experience I've ever had reading a John Green book. I really always enjoy his writing and humor, but this one just didn't do anything for me.<br/><br/><br/>I don't think the book was horrible, but it couldn't hold my attention too long so I was happy it was very short. If it was any longer I probably wouldn't have finished it. I couldn't stand Colin. He was annoying and whiny and just because he acknowledges that fact himself doesn't mean it makes it any less annoying to read about. H</span>
  <span id="freeText1698488357328410519" style="display:none"><br />This was by far the worst experience I've ever had reading a John Green book. I really always enjoy his writing and humor, but this one just didn't do anything for me.<br /><br /><br />I don't think the book was horrible, but it couldn't hold my attention too long so I was happy it was very short. If it was any longer I probably wouldn't have finished it. I couldn't stand Colin. He was annoying and whiny and just because he acknowledges that fact himself doesn't mean it makes it any less annoying to read about. His friend Hassan was alright. I didn't mind him and I thought he had some funny parts, but most of the humor with him was about his fatness and man boobs. That's not exactly my kind of humor, but I'm sure there are other people who love that kinda stuff. Lindsey wasn't that interesting either. She wasn't annoying like Colin, but I just found myself thinking they would hook up and that's it.<br /><br /><br />To me this book was just bland. It didn't have any good twists or an engaging plot. Usually I feel lots of emotions when reading one of John's books, but with this one I felt nothing but boredom. He does include his signature road trip where the character learns some lessons about life, but getting that far was a struggle for me.<br /><br />I wouldn't recommend this book to someone who wants to try John Green, because I rate this so much lower than all of his other books. The writing style and formula is present, but it's just not as good.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1698488357328410519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="NReads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34369915-nreads"><img alt="NReads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600781665p2/34369915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1040523069?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NReads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NReads" href="/user/show/34369915-nreads">NReads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1040523069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6900813640166171395"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115134._SX540_.png' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>____________________________________________<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Books are the ultimate Dumpees: put them down and they’ll wait for you forever; pay attention to them and they always love you back.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>____________________________________________<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115135._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>2 DISAPPOINTING STARS!</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://geekybookie.tumblr.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>You can find the full review and more about this book on my blog!</a><br/><br/><p>You don't know what expectations I had about this book.I have read other John Green's book like Looking for Alaska and The Fault in our Stars and really liked them especially</p></span>
  <span id="freeText6900813640166171395" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115134._SX540_.png" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Books are the ultimate Dumpees: put them down and they’ll wait for you forever; pay attention to them and they always love you back.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115135._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>2 DISAPPOINTING STARS!</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://geekybookie.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">You can find the full review and more about this book on my blog!</a><br><br><p>You don't know what expectations I had about this book.I have read other John Green's book like Looking for Alaska and The Fault in our Stars and really liked them especially the first one,also the hype about this book is insane so I thought why not.Guess I thought wrong.</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115136._SY540_.png" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>This book sure contains the marvel of John Green's smart writing,and it is so realatable,especially if you are a nerdy teen with tumblr,and that's smart and unique in a way,and I gave this book 2 stars just because of that.In the other hand it is boring,like ultimately boring.First I thought the idea with dating only girls named Katherine would be interesting or fun,but it turned out to be so dull and I really thought of not finishing this book.The only part of the book I did like was the ending and the famous John Green tumblr-ish positive message and to be honest was good.I really wanted to like this book.</p><br><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What is the point of being alive if you don't at least try to do something remarkable?” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115137._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p><b><i>The characters</i></b> were also the famous author's characters.If you are have read at least 2 books by this author,you can guess.A nerdy smart boy who happens to meet a popular unhappy girl,from who he learns about the beauty of living free and young,and also falls in love with.I did not like his sidekick,Hassan.He was annyoing and similar to some persons I do happen to know in real life,who I dislike a lot.</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115138._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p><b><i>The story</i></b> follows a boy named Colin,who is a prodigy(a really smart kid) and has this weird habit on dating only girl named Katherine.He has dated 19 Katherines and was dumbed by every single on of them.Devestated by his last break up he decides to go on a trip with his only friend,Hassan.They happen to go to this small town where they meet Lindsey,and her mother Hollis,who offers a job and a home.They decide to stay and there Colin stars his theorem about the relationships and everything start to happen in Colin's life.Things he never ecperienced before.</p><br><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I figured something out. The future is unpredictable.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419709391i/13115139._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>
  <i>I recommend this book if you are into smart books.It was so slow for me,but the ending is good and it is a positive book.If you are super into John Green's books then you should read this!</i>
</p><br><br>*Pictures from the review are not mine, I took them mostly from Google images or Tumblr*</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9594764729744382898"><b>A reenactment of the moment An Abundance of Katherines was conceived:</b><br/><br/>John Green sat at his desk, quietly contemplating the ghettoization of scrambled eggs as a breakfast food and brainstorming ideas for his new book. <br/><br/>His last novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska' title='Looking for Alaska by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Looking for Alaska</a>, had done moderately well, but he wanted to do something <i>different</i> this time. Something to show his critics that he wasn't a one-trick pony yet out-of-there enough to show his nerdfighters that he was one of them. An outsider, a man of the people.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422188919ra/13469146.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>H</span>
  <span id="freeText9594764729744382898" style="display:none"><b>A reenactment of the moment An Abundance of Katherines was conceived:</b><br><br>John Green sat at his desk, quietly contemplating the ghettoization of scrambled eggs as a breakfast food and brainstorming ideas for his new book. <br><br>His last novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>, had done moderately well, but he wanted to do something <i>different</i> this time. Something to show his critics that he wasn't a one-trick pony yet out-of-there enough to show his nerdfighters that he was one of them. An outsider, a man of the people.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422188919ra/13469146.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>His eyes drifted to a map taped on the wall, then to an unfinished Scrabble game from last night. His brother Hank had been kicking his butt, but had to leave to mediate on the metaphysics of ice-cream trucks before he could finish spelling 'hamartia' (luckily). <br><br>As he was idly staring at his unused letters, it hit him. "Eureka!" he yelled, glasses sliding down his nose in his excitement. "That's it! I'll write a book about anagrams! That's nerdy and chic, and in no way like my last protagonist's obsession with famous last words."<br><br>John picked up the letters, rearranging them in his head: 'Hem, arrow, hero. Yes, hero! He needed a protagonist. Preferably one like himself. White male, middle-class range, intelligent, quirky... but as an extra twist, his quirkiness would be the result of autism. <i>Mild</i> autism. Nothing too heavy. Fans won't be able to relate to him! Also, research is hard. I'd rather philosophize on Venn diagrams of octopi and dogs.'<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422188919ra/13469147.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Putting the letters down, he paced the floor, dialogue and plot points bombarding his head like unformed constellations. 'My protagonist should have a best friend like Colonel. Quirky enough to get his jokes, but won't overshadow the main character, which is in no way like me. Let's make him an Arab, too. That takes care of the diversity problem. And a love interest! Gorgeous and quirky. Oh, and she should exist to teach my main character an important lesson. Yay, feminism points! But how do I get them to meet?"<br><br>His gaze landed on the map again. <br><br>'A road trip! That's not like Pudge and Colonel's emotional journey to find Alaska at all!'<br><br>John laughed, clapped his hands together and sat down in front of his laptop. Then he began to write.<br><br>'John, my man, I don't know <i>how</i> you think of this stuff.'<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422188919ra/13469148.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41159819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7504388156034109487">As a YA author, I'd heard the name "John Green" whispered in the YA wind for months, but I'd never picked up one of his books until I read a synopsis for AN ABUNDANCE OF KATHERINES online. My husband, a pretty reluctant reader, snitched it from me and devoured it, so I was expecting great things.<br/><br/>I wasn't disappointed. This story of a boy struggling to come up with a theory that describes the arc of his 19 relationships with girls named Katherine was, in many places, laugh out loud funny. Even wi</span>
  <span id="freeText7504388156034109487" style="display:none">As a YA author, I'd heard the name "John Green" whispered in the YA wind for months, but I'd never picked up one of his books until I read a synopsis for AN ABUNDANCE OF KATHERINES online. My husband, a pretty reluctant reader, snitched it from me and devoured it, so I was expecting great things.<br /><br />I wasn't disappointed. This story of a boy struggling to come up with a theory that describes the arc of his 19 relationships with girls named Katherine was, in many places, laugh out loud funny. Even with flashbacks, the pacing never flagged, and though it wasn't the world's most unpredictable plot, I was never bored.<br /><br />The real charm in this book is both the characters -- larger than life, quirky people who don't quite fit into society -- and the dialog. In John Green's hands, dialog is a weapon . . . and he slayed me. <br /><br />I'm thrilled that he has a two other novels and a recent anthology for me to work through next. <br /><br />***wondering why all my reviews are five stars? Because I'm only reviewing my favorite books -- not every book I read. Consider a novel's presence on my Goodreads bookshelf as a hearty endorsement. I can't believe I just said "hearty." It sounds like a stew.***</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_127625643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127625643" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/520753-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402541317p2/520753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127625643?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/520753-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0142410705" href="/book/show/1320817.An_Abundance_of_Katherines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=mmx">mmx</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=the-kids-are-all-right">the-kids-are-all-right</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=gmba">gmba</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127625643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9931453452510620393">Colin Singleton is not a vampire or a werewolf or a sorcerer or a punning Austin zombie. He doesn’t live in a dystopian society, he hasn’t slept with his teacher. He doesn’t do drugs, his parents aren’t divorced, and he’s suffered no traumas unless you count being dumped by a slew (okay, nineteen) of girls named Katherine. <br/><br/>So, why am I reading this? I have been programmed to only care about supernatural cute boys. I call this my mid life crisis. If I give in and self analyze, I would say that I’</span>
  <span id="freeText9931453452510620393" style="display:none">Colin Singleton is not a vampire or a werewolf or a sorcerer or a punning Austin zombie. He doesn’t live in a dystopian society, he hasn’t slept with his teacher. He doesn’t do drugs, his parents aren’t divorced, and he’s suffered no traumas unless you count being dumped by a slew (okay, nineteen) of girls named Katherine. <br /><br />So, why am I reading this? I have been programmed to only care about supernatural cute boys. I call this my mid life crisis. If I give in and self analyze, I would say that I’m avoiding real life. I’m letting myself get caught up in situations that I would have daydreamed about at maybe age 12. Being the ‘damsel in distress’, being unconditionally loved for qualities that I have not yet discovered in myself. Feeling safe, always protected by really cute guys… the bad guys always get caught, and everyone lives happily ever after. <br /><br />What I’m <i> avoiding</i> is that memory of that… drive… that happens somewhere around age 16... Where you feel like you have the ability to change the world. That you will go off and do amazing things and that your whole life is waiting for you. It’s a rush. I remember sitting in the Boston Commons on summer night in 1988, I was 17, freshly graduated waiting to start college… we had just moved into an apartment in East Boston and Jimmy Cliff was playing a concert in the park. I didn’t have to tell anyone where I was going or when I would be back. I remember sitting on this hill, staring at the sky through the trees, listening to that reggae beat and thinking ‘I am free. I am young and I can do anything.’<br /><br />THAT is what I’m running from. So, when I finished <i> AAOK</i>, I almost resented Green for reminding me of that. Then, I had this selfless epiphany. This is not for me. This was written for that generation. Those kids that are getting ready to change the world. They want to ‘matter’, they want to be remembered. I really envy them. Not in that self piteous way… just in that youthful energetic way. I get this way each fall when I watch the kids slumping off to UVM. They look so hopeful and serious. Why does that have to fade? <br /><br />This is a road trip book. I’ve seen it listed as such. I would expand on that ‘road trip’ theme and make it not just a literal one. Colin wants to get away from being the dumpee of all girls named Katherine. But, it’s than that. Colin has always been considered a ‘child prodigy’ and he’s thinking that maybe that isn’t enough to ‘matter’ or to make a mark on the world. After all, a prodigy isn’t a genius… A prodigy regurgitates. A genius creates. Colin’s road trip is much more mental than led on. <br /><br />I like that Colin doesn’t sparkle or have telling scars. I picture him as a cooler Napoleon Dynamite. He has a sidekick. A pudgy Horatio. He has a talent for anagramming. And he likes math. Okay, I was all for it except for the math part. Ugh. I admit, I skimmed a lot of the theorems and graphs and algebraic equations. Lost me there. <br /><br />But, anagramming… <i>swoon</i> I am an anagramming nerd. <i> (Regard naming man, Drain Merman Gang, Ragged Man Arm Inn)</i><br /><br />Colin and his Horatio, Hassan, end up leaving Chicago and turning up in Gutshot, Tennessee. THAT is a horror story --‘dead end’ turn-- of events. I went all Ned Beatty and shuddered and almost stopped reading. But, I’m learning to fight my biases… it’s one of those mid life crisis goals. The south is NOT scary… not always. (Gutshot? Really? That was hard to swallow, I’m sure there are towns named that and all, but I’m taking baby steps here) Colin has many <b>Eureka</b> moments in Gutshot and each one makes me love him more. He’s a sweet kid who just wants to be loved, to not be left behind. Who can fault that? <br /><br />Colin quotes Democritus <i>“Everywhere man blames nature and fate, yet his fate is mostly but the echo of his character and passions, his mistakes and weaknesses.”</i><br /><br />What a great quote to pass on to Generation Z or whatever they are now. I wish that I had that when I was young. I might not have set myself up for failure… I hope that these kids carry this with them because I feel a kinship with them. I was a Reagan kid, they are Bush 34 kids… we know…<br /><br />This book really does give hope if not understanding the need for hope. (if that makes sense) I hear that there is a movie in the works. I’m sure they’ll pretty up Colin and make him seem quirky and all that, but I hope that they delve into that next level and give props to that insecurity, because that’s what we need. To see that it’s okay if you only matter to yourself. Ned Vizzini’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/248704.It_s_Kind_of_a_Funny_Story" title="It's Kind of a Funny Story by Ned Vizzini" rel="nofollow noopener">It's Kind of a Funny Story</a> had that same sort of message and I am saddened that that movie didn’t do well, that teens care more about zombies or jackasses. <br /><br /> My next <b>Eureka</b> moment: to pass this lesson on to my kids.<br /><br /><br /><u>Post Script:</u> Oh, and I want to mention that there are footnotes in this book. And it’s okay. It’s more like the DFW type footnotes where you feel like you have an extra character that you can turn to and say ‘I know, right?’… It’s all good. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9931453452510620393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer784486476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5378274911613772486">Had I been reading this on paper instead of my computer, it probably would have gone into the fireplace here: "She was incredibly hot--in that popular-girl-with-bleached-teeth-and-anorexia kind of way, which was Colin's least favorite way of being hot." And if somehow it had survived that initial immolation, I definitely would have shredded it for birdcage fodder (and I don't even own a bird!) here: "She looked prettier than she ever had before--Colin always preferred girls without makeup."<br/><br/>This </span>
  <span id="freeText5378274911613772486" style="display:none">Had I been reading this on paper instead of my computer, it probably would have gone into the fireplace here: "She was incredibly hot--in that popular-girl-with-bleached-teeth-and-anorexia kind of way, which was Colin's least favorite way of being hot." And if somehow it had survived that initial immolation, I definitely would have shredded it for birdcage fodder (and I don't even own a bird!) here: "She looked prettier than she ever had before--Colin always preferred girls without makeup."<br /><br />This book was everything I don't like about John Green. And I've already spent enough of my one precious life complaining about how his books are the literary embodiment of high school boys being unsuccessful in love and the general social hierarchy and then constructing an impossibly unpleasant wall of moral superiority as some sort of retroactive explanation for why no one likes them (they're all stupid and superficial anyway and I'm ABOVE all of that) when really maybe they're just obnoxious or plain unlucky and they can't seem to realize that - etc etc to want to spend much more time on it. Basically this is the platonic ideal of John Green books. His books teach bad lessons to fragile kids and turn them into insufferable judgmental douchebags.<br /><br />So Colin, maybe all those Katherines dumped you because you're kind of an asshole. Where's the variable for that?</span>

<div id="review_1304785" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304785" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75857-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556514715p2/75857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304785?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/75857-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who needs a fun read</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8754646054097881953">Picture this: You used to be a childhood prodigy. Member of an academic game team. You excelled in school. You were special. You met a girl named Katherine and the two of you started dating.<br/><br/>Then she dumps you.<br/><br/>Then eighteen more girls named Katherine dump you.<br/><br/>Suddenly, you're a teenager with no claim to fame except for your former status as a prodigy. No new ideas. No girl. No plans for the summer excepting wasting away in your room and moping.<br/><br/>This is not your life. But it is Colin Singleton's li</span>
  <span id="freeText8754646054097881953" style="display:none">Picture this: You used to be a childhood prodigy. Member of an academic game team. You excelled in school. You were special. You met a girl named Katherine and the two of you started dating.<br /><br />Then she dumps you.<br /><br />Then eighteen more girls named Katherine dump you.<br /><br />Suddenly, you're a teenager with no claim to fame except for your former status as a prodigy. No new ideas. No girl. No plans for the summer excepting wasting away in your room and moping.<br /><br />This is not your life. But it is Colin Singleton's life immediately after his graduation from high school.<br /><br />Given Colin's history with girls, you might not be surprised that John Green chose to name his second novel An Abundance of Katherines. <br /><br />After sulking for several days after being dumped (again), Colin is dragged out of his room by Hasan, his best friend. Hassan is confident that the only cure for Colin's depression is a road trip. So Colin and his Judge-Judy-loving, overweight, Muslim pal head off for the great beyond that is the United States between the coasts. Their road trip stops in Gutshot, Tennessee. But the adventures don't. Hired by a local bigwig to compile an oral history of Gutshot, Colin and Hassan find themselves staying with Hollis and her daughter, Lindsey. It is in Gutshot that Colin finally has what he has always wanted, a truly original idea. Thus, Colin begins to create a theorem of love in his attempt to understand his own rocky love life.<br /><br />Most of my friends who have read this book and Green's first novel Looking for Alaska agree that his second novel is not as compelling a read. Having only read "Katherines," I cannot make a judgment one way or the other. What I can say is that I loved the style of this book. There has been a growing trend to use footnotes in novels--notable examples include The Bartimaeus Trilogy by Johnathan Stroud, Jasper Fforde's Thursday Next novels, and Ibid A Life by Mark Dunn which is a novel written entirely of endnotes. Green continues that tradition here to good effect.<br /><br />The tone throughout is quirky, nerdy, and generally fun. I don't know that reading this novel will change any lives, but it will certainly get a lot of laughs. The best parts are, undoubtedly, the dialogues between Hassan and Colin. The guys are just so likable! In addition, Green's writing is snappy--all the better to keep the laughs coming. <br /><br />Like Nothing but the Truth by Justina Chen Headley, this book includes a bit of math. The "real" math behind Colin's theorem appears in the back of the book in an appendix and Green even has a website where you can use the theorem for your own relationships (if it doesn't crash your computer). Despite all of that, Green is a self-proclaimed lost cause when it comes to math. (The theorem was drafted by friend (and "resident mathematician" for Brotherhood 2.0), Daniel Biss.) I wanted to share this for a couple of reasons. First, because I think it's great that Green is writing outside of what some might call his "comfort zone" and, second, because it should illustrate that you don't have to like math to enjoy a book that features a lot of math.<br /><br />Anyway, if you need a cheerful book with some fun, lovable characters I don't think you can do better than this book which was recently nominated for the LA Times Book Award in addition to being selected as a Printz Award honor book (Looking for Alaska won the actual Printz Award, just to put that into perspective).<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my blog <a href="http://www.missprint.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Print</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8754646054097881953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19318985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19318985" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/314550-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565913182p2/314550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19318985?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/314550-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">not really sure who</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/314550-anna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/314550-anna?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19318985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2146884145015306910">I was not terribly impressed with <i>Katherines</i>. I read Green's <i>Looking For Alaska</i> and thought it was one of the best young adult novels I have ever read SO I was expecting this book to measure up to a higher standard. Unfortunately, it did not even come close. <br/><br/>Here's my beef with the book:<br/><br/><b>1) The characters.</b> I had a really hard time getting into <i>Katherines</i> because the characters were not too likable. Green gave the characters personalities, but he missed something in the character development categ</span>
  <span id="freeText2146884145015306910" style="display:none">I was not terribly impressed with <i>Katherines</i>. I read Green's <i>Looking For Alaska</i> and thought it was one of the best young adult novels I have ever read SO I was expecting this book to measure up to a higher standard. Unfortunately, it did not even come close. <br /><br />Here's my beef with the book:<br /><br /><b>1) The characters.</b> I had a really hard time getting into <i>Katherines</i> because the characters were not too likable. Green gave the characters personalities, but he missed something in the character development category that could have made his characters people that readers (especially young adults) could relate to. <br /><br /><b>2) The basic premise of the book did not appeal to me. </b>I never bought into the 19-girlfriends-named-Katherine bit and struggled to understand why the main character spent the entire novel trying to devise a mathematical formula that would explain why he was dumped so often by his girlfriends. It all just seemed a bit OCD and irrational to me, and it almost felt like he was trying too hard to come up with a unique idea for his sophomore novel.<br /><br /><b>3) I was disappointed because I found huge chunks of the book to be pretty boring. </b> Many of the conversations were dull and I found myself skimming a lot of the text. I skimmed because I kept thinking the book would make a turnaround but I think most young adult readers would probably give up. I think the footnotes and references made it worse but it just seemed to me like a lot of what happened could have been said in a simpler and faster way.<br /><br />My last concern is that I am not sure who this text is really for. Middle school kids probably would not "get" the main message because of the higher level vocabulary and I think those obscure references/footnotes make the book seem even more difficult than it is. <br /><br />I wish this book was more like <i>Looking For Alaska</i> because that was truly a fantastic read but hopefully his future writing will sort of return to that simple but beautiful type of expression. <i>Katherines</i> isn't horrible but I definitely would not go out of my way to recommend it and would suggest that you read <i>Looking For Alaska</i> instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2146884145015306910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1247503422" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247503422" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1247503422?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1247503422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3821832493111185395">So this was my first <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1406384.John_Green' title='John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Green</a> book. I get his appeal in that he can create characters that, although very different from us, can somehow resonate with our emotions and experiences. <br/><br/>I ordered this book used on Amazon, and as luck would have it before when I got an <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217274610?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>autographed</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4208569.Rainbow_Rowell' title='Rainbow Rowell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rainbow Rowell</a> book, I somehow was fortunate enough to score a first edition of this one:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429112436i/14531573._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Apparently, a first edition of one of his early books is a big deal, or so I’m told...</i><br/><br/>On to the story: we have a prodigy who has just</span>
  <span id="freeText3821832493111185395" style="display:none">So this was my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1406384.John_Green" title="John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">John Green</a> book. I get his appeal in that he can create characters that, although very different from us, can somehow resonate with our emotions and experiences. <br><br>I ordered this book used on Amazon, and as luck would have it before when I got an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217274610?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">autographed</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4208569.Rainbow_Rowell" title="Rainbow Rowell" rel="nofollow noopener">Rainbow Rowell</a> book, I somehow was fortunate enough to score a first edition of this one:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429112436i/14531573._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Apparently, a first edition of one of his early books is a big deal, or so I’m told...</i><br><br>On to the story: we have a prodigy who has just graduated high school, was dumped, and makes his way on a road trip accompanied by his best friend. Our MC, Colin is struggling with two things: understanding his recent breakup and wanting to matter in the world. Being a prodigy (<b>not</b> a genius!) he believes that he can create a formula that will be able to predict how long any given relationship will last by inputting certain factors. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429113047ra/14531707.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s this single-minded focus that blinds and consumes him. He becomes frustrated when all but one of his relationships fit into the formula.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429113047i/14531708.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Until he discovers that his recollection of that <i>one</i> relationship was all wrong. Soon he starts to realize that maybe he had been looking at <i>all</i> of them in that same way.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429113047ra/14531709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What resonated most with me about this story wasn’t the fact that Colin bemoaned his previous romances, but the fact that he <b>wanted to matter</b>; he wanted to contribute something to this world. He was a child prodigy and he plateaued and was now faced with living a mundane adulthood. I just wanted to say, “Bruh, I feel you on that. <i>You have no idea</i>.” And I think a lot of people who were once bright children, full of promise and possibility, will relate to Colin’s existential dilemma and the anxiety that comes with facing an ordinary life after an extraordinary childhood. Here we have a character about to enter college, on the precipice of entering the real world, knowing that the good years are behind him; he peaked too soon and now everything is a slow downhill crawl towards death. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429113175i/14531735.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But there’s hope in Colin’s story. He breaks the cycle of only dating Katherines and hooks up with the hot chick like the end of a John Hughes film. Maybe the future isn’t so bleak for him after all.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429113047ra/14531710.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3821832493111185395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_468131847" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468131847" />
    <a title="Scarlet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet"><img alt="Scarlet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556098025p2/3839903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468131847?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlet" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet">Scarlet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=printz-honor">printz-honor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468131847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15153639450110493147"><b>2.5</b><br/><br/>Here are some things I’ve realized after reading <i>AAoK</i>:<br/><br/>1. John Green is a talented, clever writer with a great sense of humor.<br/><br/>2. Contrary to what I’d like to think, I’m still math-phobic.<br/><br/>3. I’ll never, ever date a has-been child prodigy. Or a washed-up genius. Or a whiny guy who speaks 11 languages. Or whatever it is that Colin’s supposed to be.<br/><br/><br/><i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> is a hilarious book but it did not make me laugh. Okay, maybe a little but that was more like snorting-in-mild-amusement tha</span>
  <span id="freeText15153639450110493147" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b><br /><br />Here are some things I’ve realized after reading <i>AAoK</i>:<br /><br />1. John Green is a talented, clever writer with a great sense of humor.<br /><br />2. Contrary to what I’d like to think, I’m still math-phobic.<br /><br />3. I’ll never, ever date a has-been child prodigy. Or a washed-up genius. Or a whiny guy who speaks 11 languages. Or whatever it is that Colin’s supposed to be.<br /><br /><br /><i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> is a hilarious book but it did not make me laugh. Okay, maybe a little but that was more like snorting-in-mild-amusement than full-fledged laughing. I found the humor a little tiresome. But then, I’m the kind of girl who cracks up at things that normal people don’t find even remotely funny so maybe there’s something wrong with me and not the book.<br /><br /><i>AAoK</i> has a nerdy, heartbroken hero (irritating), some cussing in Arabic (gets taxing after a while), jokes about man-boobs and fractured balls (not really my idea of humor), a lot of math (scary) that strangely looks interesting (I wouldn’t know for sure since I skipped those parts).<br /><br />Colin really got on my nerves. Whining and theorem-making are not exactly things I’m fond of, and that’s all Colin does (in addition to spewing out random facts). I wish the narration was in first-person; it would have made things more interesting.<br /><br />The footnotes were a relief. I loved them – even the ones that had math. In fact, they were my sole motivation for trudging through the pages.<br /><br />This was my first John Green novel and well... I’m not terribly impressed. I hope <i>TFioS</i> and <i>Looking for Alaska</i> fare better.<br /><br />I’ll leave you with one of those rare lines that <i>actually</i> made me laugh:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“He tried not to sob much, because the plain fact of the matter is that boy-sobbing is exceedingly unattractive. Lindsey said, “Let it out, let it out,” and then Colin said, “But I can’t, because if I let it out it’ll sound like a bullfrog’s mating call.” ”</i>
</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15153639450110493147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494020584?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=no-one-loves-it-but-me">no-one-loves-it-but-me</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494020584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8816508664843923143">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>I may be one thousand years old, but I still love John Green books.<br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424364017ra/13752182.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I read <i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> before I even knew who John Green was. Remember - I’m 1,000, so cut me some slack people! Over the past several years it has come to my attention that almost everyone else considers this to be the lesser of all of the Green works, which had me questioning my mental state (or whether or not I was intoxicated) the first time I read th</span>
  <span id="freeText8816508664843923143" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>I may be one thousand years old, but I still love John Green books.<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424364017ra/13752182.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I read <i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> before I even knew who John Green was. Remember - I’m 1,000, so cut me some slack people! Over the past several years it has come to my attention that almost everyone else considers this to be the lesser of all of the Green works, which had me questioning my mental state (or whether or not I was intoxicated) the first time I read this book.<br><br>Okay, so I’ll grant you the premise is <i>kinda</i> snooze-a-rific. I mean, a former child prodigy who has been dumped by 19 chicks named Katherine who wants to develop something like this . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424364017i/13752183.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(*hooooooark* Ugh – just looking at that math gives me dry heaves)<br><br>in order to be able to predict who will be the dumper (or dumpee) in any relationship and when said relationship will end is not the most exciting story to be told.<br><br>And maybe Colin <i>was</i> a sitzpinkling anagramming weirdo who moped around feeling miserable about getting dumped by the umpteenth Katherine in his life, but without him I would have never had a chance to meet Hassan. Oh Hassan! I’m pretty sure he’ll go down in history as one of my favorite supporting pals. He completely stole the show. If you’ve not yet read <i>Katherines</i>, think of Hassan as younger, less dickholey, and more Muslim version of Trent from <i>Swingers</i> . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424364017ra/13752184.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Hassan is a riot, he can woo the ladies without even trying, and he refers to himself occasionally as “Daddy.” He’s the only person who was able to stop Colin from “lying facedown on the carpet” . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424364017ra/13752185.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and was the driving force in this story behind my most favorite of all plotlines . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424364017ra/13752186.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Man I love road trips! <br><br>If I were to be 100% honest, <i>Katherines</i> might not be deserving of all 5 Stars this second time around. . . but I’m not changing the rating. I love this book unapologetically and it’s still my favorite John Green – even if I’m the only one who feels that way. If nothing else, this book gave the world the following quote:<br><br><b>
  <i>“Books are the ultimate Dumpees: put them down and they’ll wait for you forever; pay attention to them and they always love you back.”</i>
</b> <br><br>And that may be good enough for a ½ Star bump on its own.<br><br>Maybe Colin wasn’t a “relatable teenager” (whatever the F that means), but at least he admitted that Holden Caulfield was a self-absorbed loser. My generation grew up with a different John who wrote characters like these . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424364017ra/13752187.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>John Green is this generation’s John Hughes and <i>everyone</i> should taste a bit of his Kool-Aid. <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424364017ra/13752188.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>You know the old saying: “Once you go Green, you never go back” . . . or something like that.<br><br>Oh and one more thing. I am <b>freaking STARVING</b> for a Monster Thickburger after reading this book. F you, Hassan!<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855168129?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andi 앤디" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andi 앤디" href="/user/show/28647266-andi">Andi 앤디</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142410707" href="/book/show/15707124-an-abundance-of-katherines">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855168129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12846451969435672567">Yup. I'm still not a John Green fan.<br/><br/>One thing I have noticed about the characters John Green creates in his novels: they're too quirky, they're smart (this one in particular has an overly smart character) and they talk in quips. NOBODY TALKS LIKE THAT IN REAL LIFE. At least not all the time. I think this is John's way of incorporating himself into his books. <br/><br/>Most YA readers see John Green as the best author ever, but his books are not that unique and his characters are the same with a few minor </span>
  <span id="freeText12846451969435672567" style="display:none">Yup. I'm still not a John Green fan.<br /><br />One thing I have noticed about the characters John Green creates in his novels: they're too quirky, they're smart (this one in particular has an overly smart character) and they talk in quips. NOBODY TALKS LIKE THAT IN REAL LIFE. At least not all the time. I think this is John's way of incorporating himself into his books. <br /><br />Most YA readers see John Green as the best author ever, but his books are not that unique and his characters are the same with a few minor tweaks. I just don't get the hype.<br /><br />However, there were some memorable parts of this book that makes it unique: Tangents and footnotes. I thought that was a very clever addition that screamed Colin. I did NOT like the repetitiveness of the word fug and the name Katherine. I now hate that name thanks to this book. Overall, this book was just sooo hard to get into... I had to force myself to keep reading hoping it will get better. Instead, this just wasted my time. I could have been reading a book more enjoyable than this one during my break. Sighhhh. <br /><br />I guess I expected so much but got a mediocre, predictable read from an author who is labelled as one of the best in YA.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_109436031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109436031" />
    <a title="Cory" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3254923-cory"><img alt="Cory" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342223197p2/3254923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109436031?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cory" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cory" href="/user/show/3254923-cory">Cory</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109436031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2586290163376451891">I've had this book sitting on my desk for two months. I'm a huge John Green fan, so you can see why this is problematic.<br/><br/>The Albuquerque library system is pretty bad. Out of all the libraries systems I've ever used, this has to be the worst. Not only does it not stock any of Justine Larbalestier's books, but it also doesn't have a decent collection of John Green's books. <br/><br/>It took me three months to get a copy of An Abundance of Katherines. It took me two months to finish it. Actually, that's a lie</span>
  <span id="freeText2586290163376451891" style="display:none">I've had this book sitting on my desk for two months. I'm a huge John Green fan, so you can see why this is problematic.<br /><br />The Albuquerque library system is pretty bad. Out of all the libraries systems I've ever used, this has to be the worst. Not only does it not stock any of Justine Larbalestier's books, but it also doesn't have a decent collection of John Green's books. <br /><br />It took me three months to get a copy of An Abundance of Katherines. It took me two months to finish it. Actually, that's a lie. I haven't finished AAoK. I'll probably never finish AAoK. But for the purpose of this review, I've read the entire novel and wasn't satisfied in the least. <br /><br />Everyone knows that John Green uses a formula. Like Sarah Dessen, most of his protagonists are the same character with different hobbies and quirks. Colin is Miles and Miles is Quentin -- only Colin likes anagramming words instead of memorizing last words. Colin, like Miles, is annoying. He only exists for the story to be funneled through him.<br /><br />John Green's protagonists are a beacon of hope for nerds everywhere in the world. While you may be unable to get a date with that hot, unattainable girl, Colin, Miles, and Quentin have dated enough hot girls to last you a lifetime -- or at least until John Green writes another book.<br /><br />His books are full of double standards. Like Kody Keplinger, author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931356.The_DUFF__Designated_Ugly_Fat_Friend_" title="The DUFF (Designated Ugly Fat Friend) by Kody Keplinger" rel="nofollow noopener">The DUFF</a>, John Green claims to present something alternative. This is a lie. The only thing that separates this from any other YA book is that our main character doesn't go through a make-over. Instead, he is accepted by the flawless pretty heroine for no reason whatsoever<br /><br />Why can't Lindsey or Margo or Alaska be anything less than gorgeous? Why can't they have goals outside of being with the protagonist? I like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>, but I think it's important to analyze these things. <br /><br />As a hero, Colin fails. Not only was I disappointed with the 3rd person narration, but I also felt like Colin lacked a soul. He wasn't a full developed character. He was a collection of quirks. I felt the same way about Miles, but at least his flaws were hidden by a cast of interesting characters. <br /><br />As a supporting character, Hassan failed in every way that Takumi and the Colonel triumphed. Takumi didn't feel like the token Asian. Hassan was without a doubt the token Arab. Hassan wasn't funny. He lacked warmth. He was just there to make bad jokes. His use of random Arabic or German was annoying. Every time he said 'kafir' or 'sitzpinkler' I rolled my eyes. Have we really gone back to the time when Mexican characters dropped random bits of Spanish into their sentences? <br /><br />Also, I didn't appreciate how his weight was used as a plot device. No, I'm not misusing that phrase. Hassan was fat for the same reason that all multi-cultural best friends are geeky, over-weight, and unappealing. It was very obvious that Green was writing for white hipster males. <br /><br />As a love interest, Lindsey just wasn't interesting. She paled in comparison to Alaska. A manic pixie must be manic, intriguing, and flawed. Lindsey wasn't. By the time she was finally introduced, I was hoping that Colin would get back with Katherine the Great. At least he would have stopped whining. <br /><br />The romance between Colin and Lindsey was yawn worthy. Even from the flashbacks, whatever Colin had with Katherine the Great moved me ten times as much. Lindsey had no personality outside of being friendly and cute. <br /><br />While the summary says this is a road trip, that is a lie. The road trip ends very quickly. The rest of the book is spent in Tennessee. Conveniently, much like Alaska, Lindsey has no accent. But she is able to put one on in the blink of an eye. <br /><br />There is no plot in this book. There is no climax. If anything, it felt like a writing exercise. We knew that Colin was going to end up with Lindsey. We knew that Hassan wasn't going to keep his girlfriend. This was too predictable, even for Green.<br /><br />I didn't mind the math, but it was only there to prove that Colin was smart. I didn't believe that he was a prodigy. He seemed like one of those whiny gifted kids that complain about being smart when in reality they're just idiots.<br /><br />I recommend skipping everything but the flashbacks. You don't need to read the rest of the story. Like the title says, this is An Abundance of Katherines, and Katherine is the only good thing about it. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2586290163376451891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2988848298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17668841840860077306">An Abundance of Katherines, John Green<br/><br/>An Abundance of Katherines is a young adult novel by John Green. Released in 2006. <br/><br/>Colin Singleton, a child prodigy, fears he will not maintain his genius as an adult. Over the span of his life, Colin has dated nineteen girls named Katherine, all spelled in that manner. After being dumped by his girlfriend, Katherine XIX, Colin is longing to feel whole, and longing to matter. ...<br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیستم ماه سپتامبر سال 2018 میلادی<br/><br/>عنوان: وفور کاترین‌ها؛ </span>
  <span id="freeText17668841840860077306" style="display:none">An Abundance of Katherines, John Green<br /><br />An Abundance of Katherines is a young adult novel by John Green. Released in 2006. <br /><br />Colin Singleton, a child prodigy, fears he will not maintain his genius as an adult. Over the span of his life, Colin has dated nineteen girls named Katherine, all spelled in that manner. After being dumped by his girlfriend, Katherine XIX, Colin is longing to feel whole, and longing to matter. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیستم ماه سپتامبر سال 2018 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: وفور کاترین‌ها؛ نویسنده: جان گرین؛ مترجم آرمان آیت‌اللهی؛ تهران آموت، ‏‫‬‏1396؛ در 288ص (296) ص؛ شابک 9786003840744؛<br /><br />نقل از پشت جلد کتاب فراوانی (وفور) کاترینها: «در روابط دختر پسری، هرکسی از یک تیپ آدمی خوشش می‌آید.؛ تیپ مورد علاقه ی «کالین سینگلتون»، شخصیتی، اخلاقی یا حتی ظاهری نیست؛ لغوی است! او از «کاترین»ها خوشش می‌آید.؛ ولی پس از اینکه نوزدهمین «کاترین» زندگیش هم، با او به هم می‌زند، تصمیم می‌گیرد انقلابی در روابط عاشقانه به پا کند...»؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 10/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1596630030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12217325642473424184"><i>Changing my rating from 2 stars to 1 star because every time I rewrite or add something to this review I'm instantly annoyed all over again.</i><br/><br/>Okay, so this is the third time I'm going to rewrite this review. Then I'm going to walk away from it forever and not look back once.<br/><br/><i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> follows Collin Singleton, who has a very specific type of dream girl. Well, I guess not really since he only really likes girls named Katherine. I don't think he really cares what they look like. It's</span>
  <span id="freeText12217325642473424184" style="display:none"><i>Changing my rating from 2 stars to 1 star because every time I rewrite or add something to this review I'm instantly annoyed all over again.</i><br /><br />Okay, so this is the third time I'm going to rewrite this review. Then I'm going to walk away from it forever and not look back once.<br /><br /><i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> follows Collin Singleton, who has a very specific type of dream girl. Well, I guess not really since he only really likes girls named Katherine. I don't think he really cares what they look like. It's like he's instantly sold on the girl because of her name. If that doesn't creep you out then I have no idea what the hell will.<br /><br />He has dated about 19 girls all named Katherine. You'd think after being dumped 19ish times that he would give up on the name and move on. Nope, so he randomly goes on a road trip with his best friend Hassan. I have no idea why they did this all of a sudden but the trip didn't make me like his character anymore than I originally did.<br /><br />Yes, he sees and learns new things. However, this entire trip, NAH the whole damn book, was constantly repetitive. I didn't think I would grow to hate words while reading a book. Yet, John Green has done that thing - so, uh thanks? <br /><br />Then there's math part of this book. Okay, it's a formula that will somehow predict when two people will break up. I almost laughed when I wrote that sentence.. WHY? Because the future is unpredictable and it took Collin basically the whole book to figure that out and then to accept it.<br /><br /><i>LE SIGH PEOPLE!</i><br /><br />Besides him obsessing over the name Katherine, he's annoying from start to finish of this book. He is constantly whining and it just annoyed me while reading. Even though he "changes" from this road trip he's still a twat to me. <br /><br />Overall, I didn't like this book. I also didn't like that I kept changing this review so many times. I didn't connect with any of the characters. Hell, I'm proud of all the Katherine's in the world that dumped him for his crazy obsession. I hope this guy sees a psychiatrist or something. He really needs one.<br /><br />I will never, repeat NEVER, reread this book ever again.<br />I will never rewrite this review ever again.<br /><br />I'm done with this book FOREVER guys. I'm completely done with everything that it's about. Am I done with John Green? Maybe. Who knows?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17083644360859760479">I'll probably be dead by morning for daring to write this about one of Green's books but boy did I loathe this book... 1,5 stars just because I enjoyed the first 40 pages and because I can't help loving John Green.<br/><br/>Okay if this book was like 500 pages long I would have quit. Fortunately, it was a short read. This is the second time I've read Green and I cannot say I was impressed with this one. I'm sure I'll take pleasure in reading the rest of his books though(I was lucky enough to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars' title='The Fault in Our Stars by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Faul</a></span>
  <span id="freeText17083644360859760479" style="display:none">I'll probably be dead by morning for daring to write this about one of Green's books but boy did I loathe this book... 1,5 stars just because I enjoyed the first 40 pages and because I can't help loving John Green.<br /><br />Okay if this book was like 500 pages long I would have quit. Fortunately, it was a short read. This is the second time I've read Green and I cannot say I was impressed with this one. I'm sure I'll take pleasure in reading the rest of his books though(I was lucky enough to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> which is one of my favourites). I had been warned that this was not a tantamount to the Fault in our Stars but I didn't see this coming. <br /><br />Even though the book is based on a good premise (nerd prodigy gets dumped by no less than 19 Katherines), there is absolutely no plot and I was unable to identify with any of the characters. I didn't like Colin (which was a real shock for me- being a nerd fan, having been a nerd myself, quoting Sheldon Coopen 24/7). He is too annoying and too self-centered for my likes. Also the ending is so predictable I wanted to kill myself once I got to the final chapter. I found the footnotes extremely distracting and utterly absurd and I hated the Math thing. Really John? Math??? Formulas? I often do the same mistake. I come across a book I like, I fall in love with the author and then I just go on to read other books by the same author. Big mistake, but I never learn. I've already purchased Looking For Alaska and I can't wait to start reading it(See? I never learn). Hopefully this one will live up to my expectations and I'll get the chance to see some of Green's great sense of humor and wit again.<br /><br />If you plan to read John Green I wouldn't recommend this book. To my mind, this felt like a waste of time. It certainly didn't make me a better person nor made me laugh. And it most certainly didn't help me overcome my Math phobia.</span>
