<div id="review_65190712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65190712" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65190712?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781423324515" href="/book/show/873584.An_Abundance_of_Katherines">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">John Green fans and those who love math and anagrams</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=printz">printz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65190712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18367789723785098582">If you are familiar with John Green, you probably already know his winning formula: a nerdy nice guy with a funny side-kick best friend, meets and falls in love with a mysterious popular but ultimately unhappy girl, then some kind of road trip ensues during which a life altering realization is achieved. <br/><br/>"An Abundance of Katherines" is no exception. Only this time the nerdy guy (Colin) is not that endearing (unlike Miles in "Looking For Alaska" or Quentin in "Paper Town"), the funny side-kick (Ha</span>
  <span id="freeText18367789723785098582" style="display:none">If you are familiar with John Green, you probably already know his winning formula: a nerdy nice guy with a funny side-kick best friend, meets and falls in love with a mysterious popular but ultimately unhappy girl, then some kind of road trip ensues during which a life altering realization is achieved. <br /><br />"An Abundance of Katherines" is no exception. Only this time the nerdy guy (Colin) is not that endearing (unlike Miles in "Looking For Alaska" or Quentin in "Paper Town"), the funny side-kick (Hassan) is not that funny, and the mysterious girl is not that mysterious or witty (compare Lindsey to Alaska and Margo). The 3rd person narration also doesn't help the cause. I think this kind of POV makes Colin unrelatable and exposes him for what he really is - a self-centered insecure super nerdy nerd whose head is full of theorems, anagrams, and numerous random facts. At some point you can't help but start thinking that if you were dating Colin, you'd break up with him just like all of his 19 ex-Katherines. <br /><br />In spite of all the flaws, the book is still moderately entertaining, the story picks up significantly in the end. And unlike "Looking For Alaska" and "Paper Towns" it has a satisfying happy (for a change) ending. "An Abundance of Katherines" is a decent read, just not as good as other John Green's books.<br /><br />Reading challenge: #1 - A</span>
  <a data-text-id="18367789723785098582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult">kids-and-young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93836698" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8489806199380892658">One of my roommates is a huge John Green fan, and after first introducing me to the series of videos he does with his brother (search "vlogbrothers" on Youtube or just watch <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TBJamfZFisU' rel='nofollow noopener'>this one</a>), she told me that I should probably read some of his books. She suggested <i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> to start with, maintaining that it's better than <i>Looking for Alaska</i> and <i>Paper Towns</i>. (incidentally, can anyone verify/disprove this claim? Just wondering)<br/><br/>So I read it, and I have to say I quite enjoyed it. And since</span>
  <span id="freeText8489806199380892658" style="display:none">One of my roommates is a huge John Green fan, and after first introducing me to the series of videos he does with his brother (search "vlogbrothers" on Youtube or just watch <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TBJamfZFisU" rel="nofollow noopener">this one</a>), she told me that I should probably read some of his books. She suggested <i>An Abundance of Katherines</i> to start with, maintaining that it's better than <i>Looking for Alaska</i> and <i>Paper Towns</i>. (incidentally, can anyone verify/disprove this claim? Just wondering)<br /><br />So I read it, and I have to say I quite enjoyed it. And since I've been watching Vlogbrothers videos for at least two months now, it felt less like I was was reading some random book and more like I was reading something written by someone I actually <i>knew</i>. Which, I'll be honest, was a little weird. But cool. <br /><br />Anyway, the book is fun, kind of silly, full of very interesting footnotes and math, and pretty damn funny. Some other reviewers have complained about the main character, Colin, but I always enjoy a socially handicapped former child prodigy. And if that socially awkward former child prodigy happens to have dated (and been dumped by) eighteen girls named Katherine and insists at one point "Love is graphable!", so much the better. His narration is also very fun. <br /><br />"When he exited the bathroom, his parents were sitting together on his bed. It was never a good sign when both his parents were in his room at the same time. Over the years it had meant:<br />1. Your grandmother/grandfather/Aunt-Suzie-whom-you-never-met-but-trust-me-she-was-nice-and-it's-a-shame is dead.<br />2. You're letting a girl named Katherine distract you from your studies.<br />3. Babies are made through an act that you will eventually find intriguing but for right now will just sort of horrify you, and also sometimes people do stuff that involves baby-making parts that does not actually involve making babies, like for instance kiss each other in places that are not on the face. <br />It never meant: <br />4. A girl nmaed Katherine called while you were in the bathtub. She's sorry. She still loves you and has made a terrible mistake and is waiting for you downstairs."</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2611728719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2611728719" />
    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2611728719?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141346090" href="/book/show/17188744-an-abundance-of-katherines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2611728719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12044478462076297410"><b>(½(2²×5²)-(6×(20)³÷(40)²)+(33-37))¼ STARS!</b> Kirkus Reviews said it best: funny and fun, challengingly complex, and entirely entertaining.<blockquote>
  <i>“You matter as much as the things that matter to you.”</i>
</blockquote>We all live for something. We all care about something. We all want to be cared about.<br/>And Colin Singleton is the most messed up: he cares about being cared about.<blockquote>What is the point of being alive if you don't at least try to do something remarkable?</blockquote>In this book, John Green tackles the whole <b>idea of wanting</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12044478462076297410" style="display:none"><b>(½(2²×5²)-(6×(20)³÷(40)²)+(33-37))¼ STARS!</b> Kirkus Reviews said it best: funny and fun, challengingly complex, and entirely entertaining.<blockquote>
  <i>“You matter as much as the things that matter to you.”</i>
</blockquote>We all live for something. We all care about something. We all want to be cared about.<br />And Colin Singleton is the most messed up: he cares about being cared about.<blockquote>What is the point of being alive if you don't at least try to do something remarkable?</blockquote>In this book, John Green tackles the whole <b>idea of wanting to be important, its implications, and effects on your life pretty amazingly.</b><blockquote>“I don't think your missing pieces ever fit inside you again once they go missing.”</blockquote>I think the best thing about it, is <b>how uniquely it approaches the “being grateful” lesson</b>. Why do I think that?<br /><br />Usually these kind of stories are about, I don't know, losing a family member or a friend or something when the character's been ungrateful for having them.<br />But in this one, John explores the idea differently: through a prodigy who, instead of appreciating the fact that he <i>is</i> a prodigy, keeps only focusing on how he's <i>not</i> a genius.<blockquote>Stories don't just make us matter to eachother—maybe they're also the only way to the infinite mattering he'd been after for so long.</blockquote>Read it with patience, pay it attention, and let yourself fall for this book. <b>It'll be a journey you'll remember, and one that's thick with mattering</b> :)<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Storyline</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>When it comes to girls (and in Colin's case, it so often did), everyone has a type. Colin Singleton's type was not physical but linguistic: he liked Katherines. And not Katies or Kats or Kitties or Cathys or Rynns or Trinas or Kays or Kates or, God forbid, Catherines. K-A-T-H-E-R-I-N-E. He had dated nineteen girls. All of them had been named Katherine. And all of them— every single solitary one—had dumped him.</i><br /><br /><b>Colin Singleton is a prodigy</b>—no, not a genuis—which means he has miraculous focus and memory, and so remembers <i>everything</i>, reads too often, and <b>dreams of being a genius</b> even more...<br /><br />To do that, he needs a discovery, a theory ... Maybe even something to help him too, as someone who never sees anything—meaning being dumped—coming.<blockquote>Colin Singleton's distance from his glasses made him realize the problem: myopia. He was nearsighted. <b>The future lay before him, inevitable but invisible.</b></blockquote>Colin has always been told how special he is as a child prodigy. But he is no longer a child—or therefore a child prodigy. <b>He wants to matter; that simple.</b><br />But it's not that simple.<blockquote>“Famous is the new popular.”</blockquote>That need is eating away at him. Slowly ruining him and all his relationships.<br />So Hassan, his amazing lazy best friend, suggests they set out on <b>a road trip, so Colin can put himself back together.</b><blockquote>“It's funny, what people will do to be remembered.”</blockquote>And there, on the road, they come upon Gutshot—and its crazy residents—and they decide to stay.<br />And that's what'll change everything :))<blockquote>We could, couldn't we? We could just keep going.</blockquote>You can, more than you even know.<br /><b>This story is about knowing what you have and being grateful for it. It's about self and life, and above all, friendship!</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Storytelling</u>
</b><blockquote>Authors never included the whole story; they just got to the point. Colin thought the truth should matter as much as the point, and he figured that was why he couldn't tell good stories.</blockquote><b>This story feels like a road trip.</b> It's not, technically; only featuring one for a short few pages. But it's still like a road trip.<br /><b>It's witty and amazing and crack-up funny. It's interesting and special and important. It's slow-burning and precious and unforgettable.</b> With a little patience and attention, you would be <i>amazed</i>.<br />It's, to sum it up, a road trip through life, with us inside of it.<blockquote>“I never did lose that reputation, but now most everyone is dead, and y'all ain't got any stories from them, so you have to believe mine by default: They were cowards, too. Everyone is.”</blockquote>The other fabulous thing about it, it's how Jon has written the <b>point of view of a prodigy</b>. One word: magnificent. Why?<br /><i>He's displayed perfectly how the mind jumps from one fact to another</i> and makes connections between so many multiple things—and sometimes even absurd ones—in the instant, as Colin registers new info or thinks of something.<br /><b>The footnotes also symbolize what happens in Colin's head tremendously</b>!<br />And besides, the facts and connections are so well chosen and impressive and laugh-out-loud hilarious, <b>embedded in the story and prose without missing a beat.</b><blockquote>“There's no romance in geometry,”<br />“Just you wait.”</blockquote>Last but not least: <b>the mathematics</b> :))<br />Beautifully tied to the story of the novel, the Theorem has absolutely made the whole thing special and <b>just something else.</b><br />It's really easy and mostly discussed in the footnotes and the appendix so is completely optional. But it's a delight nonetheless to see Colin try to tell his story through math!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Characterization</u>
</b><br /><br />As it is with John Green, the book is a character-based story that <b>gets a lot of its spark from the character development!</b><br />Let's talk about Colin Singleton, the prodigy.<blockquote>“You and me will read a book and find like three interesting things that we remember. But Colin finds <i>everything</i> intriguing. He reads a book about presidents and he remembers more of it because everything he reads clicks in his head as fugging interesting. Honestly, I've seen him do it with the phone book. He'll be like, ‘Oh, there are twenty-four listings for Tischler. How fascinating.’”</blockquote>That's how Hassan tries to explain Colin to Lindsey. It's an honourable attempt, but not quite right.<br />You see, what Hassan doesn't know is that Tischler is German for carpenter. So Colin got interested because there's this manicure place on the corner of Oakley and Lawrence called <i>24/7 Nails</i>. And he immediately wondered if there are seven carpenters of another language in the Chicago phone book. And there were seven Carpinteros!<br />Now that's hilarious, right? (OK you might not find it really interesting but it's a fun coincidence and that's all Colin needs to get interested 😂)<br /><br /><b>So here's the difference between a prodigy and a genius:</b><br />Colin thinks it's that prodigies remember history, genuises make it. Prodigies remember, geniuses do.<br />Right, Colin? Wrong.<br />Here's what I think:<br />Prodigies and genuises both <b>pay attention</b>, and they both <b>make connections between all they've noticed</b>. The difference is that while genuises don't remember everything like prodigies do, they don't just notice the thing itself; they also notice the meaning behind it.<br />So they notice twice as much as prodigies, and remember half as much. And they use that to tell a story.<br />Prodigies (at least Colin's type) only notice the fact but remember it all and use their own connections to tell the story.<br /><br />That's why Colin remembers everything. He has extraordinary focus, and is a master in linking what he observes; and we all know by now that <b>the key to remembering something is connecting it to what's already in your brain</b>.<br />It's like giving the info a tag or label so it <i>belongs</i> somewhere. Then when you want to access it, it's all organized and easy to recall!<br /><br />So Colin finds things interesting not just because of the thing itself, but because of the <i>connections</i> it has to everything else.<br /><br /><b>His only problem?</b> How he thinks prodigies either have to become genuises or fail.<br />Colin is mind-blowing with languages and decoding; and if only he understands how much he can do with that, what he can do in programming and coding and a thousand other fields <b>if he just learns to appreciate what he's got instead of constantly wanting more</b>...<br /><br />And that's what his story is about. That's what John wants to teach him and us.<blockquote>“I'm what I need to be at any given moment to day above the ground and below the radar. The only sentence that begins with ‘I’ that's true if me is I'm full of shit.”</blockquote>There's also Hassan who I LOVE, and Lindsey who terribly interests me, and the precious Holin, and The Other Colin whose addition and final role was hilarious and important :)<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Relationships</u>
</b><br /><br />While a lot of the plot and the characters' choices revolves around Colin's obsession with dating girls named Katherine—and that there's also a new romance brewing as the story processes—<b>I wouldn't call it a romantic story.</b><br /><br /><i>The romance is used as more of a way of understanding people and yourself better.</i> So it's not even written in a romantic way, except just a few special scenes. Like this.<blockquote>“The snow made it so quiet, I couldn't hear a thing in the world but you. And it was so cold then, and so silent, and I loved you so much. Now it's hot, and dead quiet again, and I love you still.”</blockquote>It also shouldn't be ignored that it makes up a great deal of the book's comedic relief—the others being Colin's and Hassan's ridiculousness 😂<blockquote>“You're such a self-involved asshole that you can't for one fugging second realize that my life doesn't spin around the star of Colin Singleton.”</blockquote>Speaking of those two—as we all know by now <b>what an expert John Green jas always been at writing friendships</b>—their relationship, and the author's exploits of it, is really one of the golden points of the whole thing!<br />So yeah, fascinating and insightful whatever angle I observe it from—and believe me, I've tried many.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Companions</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>Also by John Green:</b>

  <a href="https://www.brillianceaudio.com/product?i=11" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out this audiobook!</a>
</b><br /><br /><i>I received a hard-disc copy of this audiobook for free in exchange for my honest opinion. Full review to come.</i> <br /><br /><b>3 of 5 stars (Please read my rating system further below.</b> I think listening to this book as an audiobook really enhanced my experience while indulging in the story. Because of that, I would really like to thank Brilliance Audio for sending me a copy of the audiobook, it made me enjoy the book so much more than I would've if I had physically the book. My favorite part about this book would have to be the characters. Colin is such a smart ass who had so much more to experience in life while Hassan was just a guy who wanted to shit for the hell of it. The drastic difference between their personalities really made their quest so much more fun. I loved Colin's obsession with the fact that he needed a "Eureka" moment, it was fantastic and one of the things that I'd expect a child prodigy not to be expected because his life is literally supposed to be filled with "Eureka" moments (come on, he's a genius!!). Overall, I really liked the "finding yourself" moral/theme that the book took (I think by now that it's time that I realize that the "finding yourself" story is John Green's specialty). It's not my favorite John Green book, but it was worth the listen/read! <br /><br /><b>My rating system</b>: (I <b>do</b> use half stars.)<br /><b>5</b> - <b>I do not use the 5 star</b>. Not because a book might not be worthy, but because a book is never perfect.<br /><b>4</b> - I <b>loved</b> it! There weren't too many flaws, and I had no trouble getting through it. (A 4 star rating is the highest rating I've ever given a book.)<br /><b>3</b> - I <b>enjoyed</b> the book, but there we're flaws that made me enjoy it less.<br /><b>2</b> - I <b>finished</b> the book, but there were too many flaws for me to enjoy it.<br /><b>1</b> - I <b>could not finish</b> the book, and I probably did not finish it....</span>

<div id="review_1586306470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1586306470" />
    <a title="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages"><img alt="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585465596p2/35614518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1586306470?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chesca (thecrownedpages)" href="/user/show/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages">Chesca (thecrownedpages)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142410707" href="/book/show/15707124-an-abundance-of-katherines">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35614518-chesca-thecrownedpages?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1586306470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13795701998591566883"><b><i>“How do you just stop being terrified of getting left behind and ending up by yourself forever and not meaning anything to the world?”</i><br/><br/>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars<br/>My first John Green book!</b><br/><br/>Everyone has a type, a distinct quality or feature we are always looking for in a potential partner. Meet child prodigy Colin Singleton. He liked girls named Katherine. Not Catherine, Cathy, Kathy, Katrina, Kat, Cat, or any other variant. K-A-T-H-E-R-I-N-E.<br/><br/>John Green’s <i>
  <b>An Abundance of Katherines</b>
</i> tells the story </span>
  <span id="freeText13795701998591566883" style="display:none"><b><i>“How do you just stop being terrified of getting left behind and ending up by yourself forever and not meaning anything to the world?”</i><br /><br />Actual Rating: 3.5 stars<br />My first John Green book!</b><br /><br />Everyone has a type, a distinct quality or feature we are always looking for in a potential partner. Meet child prodigy Colin Singleton. He liked girls named Katherine. Not Catherine, Cathy, Kathy, Katrina, Kat, Cat, or any other variant. K-A-T-H-E-R-I-N-E.<br /><br />John Green’s <i>
  <b>An Abundance of Katherines</b>
</i> tells the story of Colin Singleton, a boy who’s been dumped by nineteen Katherines, leading him to work on what he called the Theorem of Underlying Katherine Predictability, in which he aimed to foresee his future relationships.<br /><br /><br /> I believe this book wasn’t what I expected it to be, yet I still enjoyed it. As a work of one of the most amazing authors of this age, I anticipated that I would have a hangover after reading it. It was a good light read. It was uncomplicated except for its math content which my brain almost wasn’t able to absorb. I’ve been wooing math for years, but it never loved me back!<br /><br />The plot was very unique. I’ve never read any contemporary romance like it. The trivia speckling the pages, especially those found at the footnotes, helped kept my interest. Learning something new every time I read is something I enjoy immensely!<br /><br />The characters weren’t flat and it’s the aspect of the story that I liked best. They each had issues they had to deal with. Colin was the kind of young man I rarely read about in books these days. He was so broken-hearted and he wasn’t afraid of showing his weakness. He was a child prodigy who had an obsession with anagramming. He was so adorable, but I understood the Katherines’ reasons for dumping him.<br /><br />Hassan, Colin’s best friend contributed most in making this a hilarious read. Together, Colin and Hassan were just epic. I loved that they could communicate with each other in different languages and that they could come up with words that only they would understand.<br /><br />Lindsey Lee Wells was a very honest character. She exhibited how complex any individual could be. She had different personalities or masks she had to put on for every group of people she met. She was dating the popular guy and went with his crowd, but it was as if she didn’t really belong with them.<br /><br />What I didn’t like that much with how the story flowed was that the climax wasn’t that apparent. It was as if feeling for a nail on a flat wooden surface, but it was hammered too hard that you could not find it with just the touch of your fingertips.<br /><br />Although the plot twists were not mind-blowing, I love how they led to such a lovely ending that opened to new beginnings. It was filled with new things and hope for each of the significant characters.<br /><br />Overall, I think everyone who’s ever been in love should check this out. I highly recommended it to math nerds and anagram nerds.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13795701998591566883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_14189749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14189749" />
    <a title="Krissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32158-krissa"><img alt="Krissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569946863p2/32158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14189749?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krissa" href="/user/show/32158-krissa">Krissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14189749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11873996609777610507">I think I already said this in a review but I might just need a break from young adult fiction, because everyone I know who reads YA raved about this novel and I read it from cover to cover without once really engaging, and with far too many inward groans and eye-rolls.<br/><br/>I mean, for starters, the quirky teenaged characters were, um, very quirky. Very reliably quirky. Everyone had their schtick and everyone talked like they were in a Joss Wheden show. And hey, I LOVE Joss Whedon but it's a differen</span>
  <span id="freeText11873996609777610507" style="display:none">I think I already said this in a review but I might just need a break from young adult fiction, because everyone I know who reads YA raved about this novel and I read it from cover to cover without once really engaging, and with far too many inward groans and eye-rolls.<br /><br />I mean, for starters, the quirky teenaged characters were, um, very quirky. Very reliably quirky. Everyone had their schtick and everyone talked like they were in a Joss Wheden show. And hey, I LOVE Joss Whedon but it's a different animal altogether when you're reading it. And by "different animal" I mean "sort of annoying after a while". For another, the book kept trying to TEACH me. Always be yourself! Think about your choices! I'm not seventeen so these messages are, well, I'm a little old for them. And christ, every other word was "fugging" and after a while you just want someone to unleash a decent FUCK to get the party started.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, the plot was original albeit a little contrived and there was definitely enough awkwardly endearing teenage moments for it to be funny and authentic. And there's nothing worse than an inauthentic YA novel so for that alone, I give Green massive kudos. If I were seventeen I would have lapped this shit right up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11873996609777610507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('19hEuZrWjAfNPWQJzw8tcdrEBFhBHZESjGv0rRMJ9Mbt/i1rIYhFb2oW0Gg4+ieuDJvjkI+QH3XXFbIc3koGXA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ch0vMKkWzM+eCWv2VB8YiUMXJNUxYXJZcQwjA0aWC04wO0biEkgFpzki35ej6hJWlUjDHf/s/D4qcmWyi9X51A==')})
  }

Maybe some people are just meant to be in the same story.&quot;\n\n\nAt first, Jude and her twin brother Noah, are inseparable. Noah draws constantly and is falling in love with the charismatic boy next door, while daredevil Jude wears red-red lipstick, cliff-dives, and does all the talking for both of them. Years later, they are barely speaking. Something has happened to change the twins in different yet equally devastating ways . . . but then Jude meets an intriguing, irresistible boy and a mysterious new mentor. The early years are Noah\'s to tell; the later years are Jude\'s. But they each have only half the story, and if they can only find their way back to one another, they\'ll have a chance to remake their world. This radiant, award-winning novel from the acclaimed author of The Sky Is Everywhere will leave you breathless and teary and laughing—often all at once.\n\nPrintz Award Winner Stonewall Honor       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1406384.John_Green">About John Green</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1406384.John_Green"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1353452301p3/1406384.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6780560281344696719"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>John Green's first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska' title='Looking for Alaska by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Looking for Alaska</a>, won the 2006 Michael L. Printz Award presented by the American Library Association. His second novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49750.An_Abundance_of_Katherines' title='An Abundance of Katherines by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Abundance of Katherines</a>, was a 2007 Michael L. Printz Award Honor Book and a finalist for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize. His next novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2914097.Paper_Towns' title='Paper Towns by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paper Towns</a>, is a New </span>
  <span id="freeText6780560281344696719" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />John Green's first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>, won the 2006 Michael L. Printz Award presented by the American Library Association. His second novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49750.An_Abundance_of_Katherines" title="An Abundance of Katherines by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">An Abundance of Katherines</a>, was a 2007 Michael L. Printz Award Honor Book and a finalist for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize. His next novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2914097.Paper_Towns" title="Paper Towns by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a>, is a New York Times bestseller and won the Edgar Allen Poe Award for Best YA Mystery. In January 2012, his most recent novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>, was met with wide critical acclaim, unprecedented in Green's career. The praise included rave reviews in Time Magazine and The New York Times, on NPR, and from award-winning author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11466.Markus_Zusak" title="Markus Zusak" rel="nofollow noopener">Markus Zusak</a>. The book also topped the New York Times Children's Paperback Bestseller list for several weeks. Green has also coauthored a book with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" title="David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a>, published in 2010. The film rights for all his books, with the exception of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson Will Grayson</a>, have been optioned to major Hollywood Studios.<br /><br />In 2007, John and his brother Hank were the hosts of a popular internet blog, "<a href="http://www.brotherhood2.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Brotherhood 2.0</a>," where they discussed their lives, books and current events every day for a year except for weekends and holidays. They still keep a video blog, now called "The Vlog Brothers," which can be found on the <a href="http://nerdfighters.ning.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Nerdfighters</a> website, or a direct link <a href="http://youtube.com/vlogbrothers" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6780560281344696719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
